<p><b>Veracruz</b> (<small>American Spanish: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[beɾaˈkɾus]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata"> (<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:VeracruzPronunciation.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a> </span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/16/VeracruzPronunciation.ogg" title="VeracruzPronunciation.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small>), formally <b>Veracruz de Ignacio de la Llave</b> (<small>American Spanish: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[beɾaˈkɾus ðe iɣˈnasjo ðe la ˈʝaβe]</a></span>), officially the <b>Free and Sovereign State of Veracruz de Ignacio de la Llave</b> (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <span lang="es"><i>Estado Libre y Soberano de Veracruz de Ignacio de la Llave</i></span>), is one of the 31 states that, along with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexico_city" title="Mexico city">Federal District</a>, comprise the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Political_divisions_of_Mexico" title="Political divisions of Mexico">32 federative entities</a> of <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>. It is divided in <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Veracruz" title="Municipalities of Veracruz">212 municipalities</a> and its capital city is <a href="/wiki/Xalapa" title="Xalapa">Xalapa-Enríquez</a>.</p>
<p>Veracruz is bordered by the states of <a href="/wiki/Tamaulipas" title="Tamaulipas">Tamaulipas</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/San_Luis_Potos%C3%AD" title="San Luis Potosí">San Luis Potosí</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hidalgo_(state)" title="Hidalgo (state)">Hidalgo</a> to the west, <a href="/wiki/Puebla" title="Puebla">Puebla</a> to the southwest, <a href="/wiki/Oaxaca" title="Oaxaca">Oaxaca</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chiapas" title="Chiapas">Chiapas</a> to the south, and <a href="/wiki/Tabasco" title="Tabasco">Tabasco</a> to the southeast. On its east, Veracruz has a significant share of the coastline of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>.</p>
<p>The state is noted for its mixed ethnic and indigenous populations. Its <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Veracruz" title="Cuisine of Veracruz">cuisine</a> reflects the many cultural influences that have come through the state because of the importance of the port of Veracruz.</p>
<p>In addition to the capital city, the state's largest cities include <a href="/wiki/Veracruz_(city)" title="Veracruz (city)">Veracruz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coatzacoalcos" title="Coatzacoalcos">Coatzacoalcos</a>, <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba,_Veracruz" title="Córdoba, Veracruz">Córdoba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minatitl%C3%A1n,_Veracruz" title="Minatitlán, Veracruz">Minatitlán</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Poza_Rica,_Veracruz" title="Poza Rica, Veracruz">Poza Rica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boca_del_R%C3%ADo,_Veracruz" title="Boca del Río, Veracruz">Boca Del Río</a> and <a href="/wiki/Orizaba" title="Orizaba">Orizaba</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Veracruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The full name of the state is Veracruz de Ignacio de la Llave. Veracruz was named after the city of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Veracruz,_Veracruz" title="Veracruz, Veracruz">Veracruz</a> (From <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> <i>Vera Crux</i>, "<a href="/wiki/True_Cross" title="True Cross">True Cross</a>"), which was originally called the <b>Villa Rica de la Vera Cruz</b>. The suffix is in honor of <a href="/wiki/Ignacio_de_la_Llave" title="Ignacio de la Llave">Ignacio de la Llave y Segura Zevallos</a> (1818–1863), who was the governor of the Veracruz from 1861 to 1862. The state’s seal was authorized by the state legislature in 1954, adapting the one used for the port of Veracruz and created by the Spanish in the early 16th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nomenclatura_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-nomenclatura-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Veracruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_geography">Political geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Veracruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Political geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The state is a crescent-shaped strip of land wedged between the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Madre_Oriental" title="Sierra Madre Oriental">Sierra Madre Oriental</a> to the west and the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a> to the east.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-khursh_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-khursh-11">[11]</a></sup> Its total area is 78,815 km<sup>2</sup> (30,431 sq mi), accounting for about 3.7% of Mexico’s total territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-esveracruz_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-esveracruz-12">[12]</a></sup> It stretches about 650 km (403.9 mi) north to south, but its width varies from between 212 km (132 mi) to 36 km (22 mi), with an average of about 100 km (62 mi) in width.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediofisico_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-mediofisico-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brittanica_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-brittanica-14">[14]</a></sup> Veracruz shares common borders with the states of <a href="/wiki/Tamaulipas" title="Tamaulipas">Tamaulipas</a> (to the north), <a href="/wiki/Oaxaca" title="Oaxaca">Oaxaca</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chiapas" title="Chiapas">Chiapas</a> (to the south), <a href="/wiki/Tabasco" title="Tabasco">Tabasco</a> (to the southeast), and <a href="/wiki/Puebla" title="Puebla">Puebla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hidalgo_(state)" title="Hidalgo (state)">Hidalgo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/San_Luis_Potos%C3%AD" title="San Luis Potosí">San Luis Potosí</a> (on the west). Veracruz has 690 km (429 mi) of coastline with the Gulf of Mexico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schmal_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-schmal-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_geography">Natural geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Veracruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Natural geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Citlaltepetl.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Citlaltepetl.jpg/220px-Citlaltepetl.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Citlaltepetl.jpg/330px-Citlaltepetl.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Citlaltepetl.jpg/440px-Citlaltepetl.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Citlaltepetl.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Pico_de_Orizaba" title="Pico de Orizaba">Pico de Orizaba</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The natural geography can be categoried into nine regions: The Sierra de Zongolica, the Tecolutla Region, the Huayacocotla Region, the Metlac River area, the Tuxtlas Region, the Central Region, the Laguna del Castillo Region, the Pueblo Viejo-Tamiahua Region and the Laguna de Alvarado Region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediofisico_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-mediofisico-13">[13]</a></sup> The topography changes drastically, rising from the narrow coastal plains to the highlands of the eastern Sierra Madre. Elevation varies from sea level to the <a href="/wiki/Pico_de_Orizaba" title="Pico de Orizaba">Pico de Orizaba</a>, Mexico’s highest peak at 5,636 m (18,491 ft) above sea level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-esveracruz_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-esveracruz-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schmal_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-schmal-15">[15]</a></sup> The coast consists of low sandy strips interspersed with tidewater streams and lagoons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brittanica_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-brittanica-14">[14]</a></sup> Most of the long coastline is narrow and sandy with unstable dunes, small shifting lagoons and points.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediofisico_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-mediofisico-13">[13]</a></sup> The mountains are of the Sierra Madre Oriental and the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Mexican_Volcanic_Belt" title="Trans-Mexican Volcanic Belt">Trans-Mexican Volcanic Belt</a>. Mountain ranges include the Sierra de Topila, Sierra de Otontepec, Sierra de Huayacocotla, Sierra de Coxquihui, Sierra de Chiconquiaco, Sierra de Jalacingo, Sierra de Axocuapan, Sierra de Huatusco, Sierra de Zongolica and the Sierra de Los Tuxtla. Major peaks include Pico de Orizaba (5,636 m, 18,491 ft), <a href="/wiki/Cofre_de_Perote" title="Cofre de Perote">Cofre de Perote</a> (4,282 m, 14,048.6 ft), Cerro de Tecomates (3,227 m, 10,587 ft), Cerro del Vigía Alta (3,055 m, 10,023 ft) and Cerro de 3 Tortas (2,997 m, 9,833 ft). The Pico de Orizaba is covered in snow year round; the Cofre de Perote is covered in winter. Major valleys include the Acultzingo, Córdoba, Maltrata, Orizaba and San Andrés.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediofisico_13-3"><a href="#cite_note-mediofisico-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:JamapaRiver-Near_CasaBlancaTown_VeracruzMexico.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/JamapaRiver-Near_CasaBlancaTown_VeracruzMexico.jpg/220px-JamapaRiver-Near_CasaBlancaTown_VeracruzMexico.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/JamapaRiver-Near_CasaBlancaTown_VeracruzMexico.jpg/330px-JamapaRiver-Near_CasaBlancaTown_VeracruzMexico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/JamapaRiver-Near_CasaBlancaTown_VeracruzMexico.jpg/440px-JamapaRiver-Near_CasaBlancaTown_VeracruzMexico.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:JamapaRiver-Near_CasaBlancaTown_VeracruzMexico.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Jamapa_River" title="Jamapa River">Jamapa River</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>More than 40 rivers and tributaries provide water for irrigation and hydroelectric power; they also carry rich silt down from the eroding highlands, which is deposited in the valleys and coastal areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brittanica_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-brittanica-14">[14]</a></sup> All of the rivers and streams that cross the state begin in the Sierra Madre Oriental or in the Central Mesa, flowing east to the Gulf of Mexico. The important ones include: <a href="/wiki/Actopan_River" title="Actopan River">Actopan River</a>, Acuatempan river, Río Blanco, <a href="/wiki/Cazones_River" title="Cazones River">Cazones River</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coatzacoalcos_River" title="Coatzacoalcos River">Coatzacoalcos River</a>, Río de La Antigua, Hueyapan River, <a href="/wiki/Jamapa_River" title="Jamapa River">Jamapa River</a>, Nautla River, <a href="/wiki/P%C3%A1nuco_River" title="Pánuco River">Pánuco River</a>, <a href="/wiki/Papaloapan_River" title="Papaloapan River">Papaloapan River</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tecolutla_River" title="Tecolutla River">Tecolutla River</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tonal%C3%A1_River" title="Tonalá River">Tonalá River</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tuxpan_River_(Veracruz)" title="Tuxpan River (Veracruz)">Tuxpan River</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Xoloapa_River&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Xoloapa River (page does not exist)">Xoloapa River</a>. The largest in terms of water discharge are the Pánuco, Tuxpan, Papaloapan, Coazocoalcos and <a href="/wiki/Uspanapa_River" title="Uspanapa River">Uxpanapa</a>. The Panuco, Tuxpan, Papaloapan and Coatzacoalcos are navigable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediofisico_13-4"><a href="#cite_note-mediofisico-13">[13]</a></sup> Two of Mexico's most polluted rivers, the Coatzacoalcos and the Río Blanco are located in the state. Much of the pollution comes from industrial sources, but the discharge of sewerage and uncontrolled garbage disposal are also major contributors. The state has very few sewage treatment plants, with only 10% of sewage being treated before discharge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dosrios_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-dosrios-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>The state also has ten major waterfalls and ten major coastal lagoons. There is only one significant lake, called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lake_Catemaco" title="Lake Catemaco">Lake Catemaco</a>. Off the coast are the islands of Isla de Lobos, Isla de los Burros, <a href="/wiki/Isla_de_Sacrificios" title="Isla de Sacrificios">Isla de Sacrificios</a>, Isla de Salmendina, Isla del Idolo, Isladel Toro, Isla Frijoles, Isla Juan A Ramirez, Isla Pajaros and Isla Terrón and the ocean reefs called Blanquilla, Medio, Tangüillo, Tuxpan, Gualleguilla, Gallega, Anegada de Adento Anegada de Afuera and Cabezo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediofisico_13-5"><a href="#cite_note-mediofisico-13">[13]</a></sup></p>

<p>The large variation of altitude results in a large mixture of climates, from cold, snow-topped mountain peaks to warm wet tropical areas on the coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schmal_15-2"><a href="#cite_note-schmal-15">[15]</a></sup> 32% of the state is classified as hot and humid, 52% as hot and semi humid, 9% is warm and humid, 6% as temperate and humid and 1% is classified as cold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-esveracruz_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-esveracruz-12">[12]</a></sup> Hot and humid and hot and semi-humid climates dominate from sea level to about 1,000 m (3,280.8 ft) above sea level. Average annual temperature ranges from 22 to 26C with precipitation varying from 2,000 mm (78.7 in) to just over 3,500 mm (137.8 in) per year. Cooler and humid climates are found at elevations between 1,000 m (3,280.8 ft) and 1,600 m (5,249.3 ft). These have an average temperature of between 18 and 22C with precipitation varying between 2,000 mm (78.7 in) and 2,500 mm (98.4 in). Temperate climates are found at higher altitudes, between 1,600 m (5,249.3 ft) and 2,800 m (9,186.4 ft). Temperatures here vary from 12 to 18C with precipitation varying more, between 500 mm (19.7 in) and 2,500 mm (98.4 in). Cold climates are found at the highest elevations, reaching up to the Cofre de Perote and the Pico de Orizaba. There is a small semi arid region around the city of Perote and the west of the Huasteca area. This is due to a <a href="/wiki/Rain_shadow" title="Rain shadow">rain shadow</a> caused by the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Mexican_Volcanic_Belt" title="Trans-Mexican Volcanic Belt">Trans-Mexican Volcanic Belt</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Madre_Oriental" title="Sierra Madre Oriental">Sierra Madre Oriental</a>, which do not permit the flow of moist Gulf air to this region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediofisico_13-6"><a href="#cite_note-mediofisico-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecosystems">Ecosystems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Veracruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Ecosystems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Laguna_catemaco_shore.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Laguna_catemaco_shore.jpg/220px-Laguna_catemaco_shore.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Laguna_catemaco_shore.jpg/330px-Laguna_catemaco_shore.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Laguna_catemaco_shore.jpg/440px-Laguna_catemaco_shore.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Laguna_catemaco_shore.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Shore of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lake_Catemaco" title="Lake Catemaco">Lake Catemaco</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Various types of forest cover the state, but evergreen <a href="/wiki/Tropical_forest" title="Tropical forest">tropical forest</a> dominate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediofisico_13-7"><a href="#cite_note-mediofisico-13">[13]</a></sup> The state’s ecoregion is of great importance for many plant and animal species. It is a center of plant endemism and has two separate endemic bird areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWF_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-WWF-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>The northern part of the state as well as the higher mountain areas, are convergence zones between lowland evergreen tropical forests and more temperate flora and fauna. It is also the northernmost occurrence of subhumid tropical forest in Mexico, although little of this remains, mostly on steep slopes. This tropical forest is situated in the northeastern coastal plain and extends into southern Tamaulipas state, on the east side of the Sierra Madre Oriental. The soils here are volcanic and shallow, but with rich organic matter. Species that predominate include Mayan breadnut (<a href="/wiki/Brosimum_alicastrum" title="Brosimum alicastrum">Brosimum alicastrum</a>), sapodilla (<a href="/wiki/Manilkara_zapota" title="Manilkara zapota">Manilkara zapota</a>), rosadillo (<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Celtis_monoica&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Celtis monoica (page does not exist)">Celtis monoica</a>), <a href="/wiki/Bursera_simaruba" title="Bursera simaruba">Bursera simaruba</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Dendropanax_arboreus&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Dendropanax arboreus (page does not exist)">Dendropanax arboreus</a>, and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sideroxylon_capiri&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sideroxylon capiri (page does not exist)">Sideroxylon capiri</a>. This ecoregion extends into the central part of the state, with vegetation changing to include mahogany (<a href="/wiki/Swietenia_macrophylla" title="Swietenia macrophylla">Swietenia macrophylla</a>), sapodilla (<a href="/wiki/Manilkara_zapota" title="Manilkara zapota">Manilkara zapota</a>), <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Bernoullia_flammea&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Bernoullia flammea (page does not exist)">Bernoullia flammea</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Astronium_graveolens" title="Astronium graveolens">Astronium graveolens</a> .<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWF_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-WWF-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Veracruz has been described as having one of the richest varieties of wildlife in the western hemisphere. There is an especially diverse array of endemic insects like the conspicuous <i><a href="/wiki/Arsenura_armida" title="Arsenura armida">Arsenura armida</a></i>. As well as insects, the state is known for its many arachnids, and features over 25 species of <a href="/wiki/Tarantula" title="Tarantula">tarantula</a> (Theraphosidae), of which many are endemic. The state is part of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Birdlife_International" title="Birdlife International">Birdlife International</a>’s Endemic Bird Area(EBA) project due to the number of endemic birds here. Some of these include green-cheeked amazon (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amazona_viridigenalis" title="Amazona viridigenalis">Amazona viridigenalis</a>), Tamaulipas crow (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Corvus_imparatus" title="Corvus imparatus">Corvus imparatus</a>), Altamira yellowthroat (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geothlypis_flavovelata" title="Geothlypis flavovelata">Geothlypis flavovelata</a>) and crimson-collared grosbeak (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhodothraupis_celaeno" title="Rhodothraupis celaeno">Rhodothraupis celaeno</a>). Despite much of the deterioration of the forest areas, it is still an important stopover for migratory birds as well. Many endangered mammal species can be found here including two endemic rodents (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peromyscus_ochraventer" title="Peromyscus ochraventer">Peromyscus ochraventer</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neotoma_angustapalata" title="Neotoma angustapalata">Neotoma angustapalata</a>), the jaguar (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Panthera_onca" title="Panthera onca">Panthera onca</a>), ocelot (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leopardus_pardalis" title="Leopardus pardalis">Leopardus pardalis</a>), jaguarundi (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Herpailurus_yaguarondi" title="Herpailurus yaguarondi">Herpailurus yaguarondi</a>) and coati (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nasua_narica" title="Nasua narica">Nasua narica</a>) .<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWF_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-WWF-17">[17]</a></sup> The endangered <a href="/wiki/Baird%27s_tapir" title="Baird's tapir">Baird's tapir</a> may occasionally be spotted in the state's southern jungle regions, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bi%C3%B3sfera_Los_Tuxtlas" title="Biósfera Los Tuxtlas">Biósfera Los Tuxtlas</a>. This region is also the northernmost extent of the primate Alouatta palliata, or <a href="/wiki/Mantled_howler" title="Mantled howler">mantled howler</a>.</p>
<p>Most of Veracruz’s native <a href="/wiki/Veracruz_moist_forests" title="Veracruz moist forests">forests</a> have been destroyed and replaced by scrub and secondary communities of trees. From 1900 to 1987, over 18,553 km<sup>2</sup> (7,163.4 sq mi) of forest had been logged, resulting in the loss of habitat and biodiversity. Much of the logging is due to commercial timber, search for tropical hardwoods and the clearing of land for local farmers, especially for cattle grazing. Only 20% of Veracruz’s original ecosystem remains, with 64% transformed by human exploitation. Despite some efforts at conservation and reclamation, exploitation continues to put pressure on remaining wild areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWF_17-3"><a href="#cite_note-WWF-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Buganvilia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="467" data-file-width="604" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Buganvilia.jpg/220px-Buganvilia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Buganvilia.jpg/330px-Buganvilia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Buganvilia.jpg/440px-Buganvilia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Buganvilia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bougainvillea.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The state has 31 environmentally protected areas in 21 different municipalities. Nine are urban parks, three are national parks (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pico_de_Orizaba_National_Park" title="Pico de Orizaba National Park">Pico de Orizaba</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cofre_de_Perote_National_Park" title="Cofre de Perote National Park">Cofre de Perote</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=San_Jos%C3%A9_de_los_Molinos_National_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="San José de los Molinos National Park (page does not exist)">San José de los Molinos</a> .<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediofisico_13-8"><a href="#cite_note-mediofisico-13">[13]</a></sup> The Cofre de Perote National Park is 11,700 hectares of pine and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oyamel" title="Oyamel">oyamel</a> forest, which was created in 1937. The <a href="/wiki/Los_Tuxtlas" title="Los Tuxtlas">Los Tuxtlas</a> Biosphere Reserve covers the municipalities of <a href="/wiki/%C3%81ngel_R._Cabada_(municipality)" title="Ángel R. Cabada (municipality)">Ángel R. Cabada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Tuxtla" title="Santiago Tuxtla">Santiago Tuxtla</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Andres_Tuxtla" title="San Andres Tuxtla">San Andres Tuxtla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catemaco" title="Catemaco">Catemaco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soteapan" title="Soteapan">Soteapan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mecayapan" title="Mecayapan">Mecayapan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pajapan" title="Pajapan">Pajapan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tatahuicapan" title="Tatahuicapan">Tatahuicapan</a> for a total of 155,122 ha (383,314.8 acres). It contains various volcanos such as San Martín and Santa Marta and rich biodiversity as it stretches from sea level to higher elevations, with 16 climate regions groups into four climate types. Forest types range from evergreen tropical rainforest to pine. 75% of species here are also found in <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central America</a> and there is a total of 2,368 plant species. Some, such as <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Costus_dirzoi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Costus dirzoi (page does not exist)">Costus dirzoi</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Daphnopsis_megacarpa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Daphnopsis megacarpa (page does not exist)">Daphnopsis megacarpa</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Eugenia_sotoesparzae&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Eugenia sotoesparzae (page does not exist)">Eugenia sotoesparzae</a>, <a href="/wiki/Inga_sinacae" title="Inga sinacae">Inga sinacae</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Miconia_ibarrae&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Miconia ibarrae (page does not exist)">Miconia ibarrae</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mormodes_tuxtlensis&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mormodes tuxtlensis (page does not exist)">Mormodes tuxtlensis</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Thelypteris_rachyflexuosa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Thelypteris rachyflexuosa (page does not exist)">Thelypteris rachyflexuosa</a>, are native only to this area. Wildlife includes 102 mammal species, 49 amphibian, 109 reptilian, 561 bird species and more. Species in danger of extinction include the jaguar, <a href="/wiki/Spider_monkey" title="Spider monkey">spider monkey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anteater" title="Anteater">anteater</a> .<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediofisico_13-9"><a href="#cite_note-mediofisico-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sistema_Arrecifal_Veracruzano_National_Marine_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sistema Arrecifal Veracruzano National Marine Park (page does not exist)">The Veracruz Reef System</a> is also considered to be a national park and is mostly off the coast of Veracruz city, <a href="/wiki/Boca_del_R%C3%ADo,_Veracruz" title="Boca del Río, Veracruz">Boca del Río</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alvarado,_Veracruz" title="Alvarado, Veracruz">Alvarado</a>. The area includes coral reefs, seaweed beds and other marine vegetation, covering an area of 52,239 ha (129,085.4 acres). There are seventeen reefs in total, some of which jut above the surface to form small islands. This system links with the reef systems of <a href="/wiki/Campeche" title="Campeche">Campeche</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n_(state)" title="Yucatán (state)">Yucatán</a> .<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediofisico_13-10"><a href="#cite_note-mediofisico-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Veracruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Columbian">Pre-Columbian</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Veracruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Pre-Columbian">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Olmec_Head_from_San_Lorenzo,_Veracruz.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2272" data-file-width="1704" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Olmec_Head_from_San_Lorenzo%2C_Veracruz.jpg/220px-Olmec_Head_from_San_Lorenzo%2C_Veracruz.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Olmec_Head_from_San_Lorenzo%2C_Veracruz.jpg/330px-Olmec_Head_from_San_Lorenzo%2C_Veracruz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Olmec_Head_from_San_Lorenzo%2C_Veracruz.jpg/440px-Olmec_Head_from_San_Lorenzo%2C_Veracruz.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Olmec_Head_from_San_Lorenzo,_Veracruz.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Olmec stone head</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The history of the native peoples of the state of Veracruz is complex. In the pre-Columbian period, the modern-day state of Veracruz was inhabited primarily by four indigenous cultures. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Huasteca" title="Huasteca">Huastecs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Otomi_people" title="Otomi people">Otomis</a> occupied the north, while the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Totonac" title="Totonac">Totonacs</a> resided in the north-center. The <a href="/wiki/Olmec" title="Olmec">Olmecs</a>, one of the oldest cultures in the Americas, became dominant in the southern part of Veracruz.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schmal_15-3"><a href="#cite_note-schmal-15">[15]</a></sup> Remains of these past civilizations can be found in archeological sites such as Pánuco, <a href="/wiki/Castillo_de_Teayo_(Mesoamerican_site)" title="Castillo de Teayo (Mesoamerican site)">Castillo de Teayo</a>, El Zapotal, Las Higueras, Quiahuiztlán, <a href="/wiki/El_Taj%C3%ADn" title="El Tajín">El Tajín</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cempoala" title="Cempoala">Cempoala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tres_Zapotes" title="Tres Zapotes">Tres Zapotes</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Lorenzo_Tenochtitl%C3%A1n" title="San Lorenzo Tenochtitlán">San Lorenzo Tenochtitlán</a> .<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enchistoria_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-enchistoria-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first major civilization in the territory of the current state was that of the Olmecs. The Olmecs lived in the <a href="/wiki/Coatzacoalcos_River" title="Coatzacoalcos River">Coatzacoalcos River</a> region and it became the center of Olmec culture. The main ceremonial center here was San Lorenzo Tenochtitlán. Other major centers in the state include Tres Zapotes in the city of Veracruz and <a href="/wiki/La_Venta" title="La Venta">La Venta</a> in Tabasco. The culture reached its height about 2600 years ago, with its best-known artistic expression being the <a href="/wiki/Olmec_colossal_heads" title="Olmec colossal heads">colossal stone heads</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enchistoria_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-enchistoria-18">[18]</a></sup> These ceremonial sites were the most complex of that early time period. For this reason, many anthropologists consider the Olmec civilization to be the mother culture of the many Mesoamerican cultures that followed it. By 300 BCE, this culture was eclipsed by other emerging civilizations in Mesoamerica.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schmal_15-4"><a href="#cite_note-schmal-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Another major group was the Totonacs, who have survived to the present day. Their region, called <a href="/wiki/Totonacapan" title="Totonacapan">Totonacapan</a>, is centered between the Cazones River and the Papaloapan River in the north of the state. Pre-Columbian Totonacs lived from hunting, fishing and agriculture, mostly of corn, beans, chili peppers and squash. This is also the native region of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vanilla_bean" title="Vanilla bean">vanilla bean</a>. Clay sculptures with smiling faces are indicative of this culture. The major site is <a href="/wiki/El_Taj%C3%ADn" title="El Tajín">El Tajín</a>, located near <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Papantla,_Veracruz" title="Papantla, Veracruz">Papantla</a>, but the culture reached its apogee in Cempoala (about five miles (8 km) inland from the current port of Veracruz), when it was conquered by the Aztecs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enchistoria_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-enchistoria-18">[18]</a></sup> When the Spaniards arrived in 1519, the territory was still home to a population of about 250,000 people living in fifty population centers and speaking four Totonac dialects. 25,000 were living in Cempoala alone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schmal_15-5"><a href="#cite_note-schmal-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Huastec_people" title="Huastec people">Huastecs</a> are in the far north of the Veracruz and extend into parts of Tamaulipas, Hidalgo, San Luis Potosí, <a href="/wiki/Quer%C3%A9taro" title="Querétaro">Querétaro</a> and Puebla. The language and agricultural techniques of these people and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mayan_peoples" title="Mayan peoples">Maya</a> are similar; however, only a few buildings and ceramics remain from the early Huastec culture. This culture also reached its peak between 1200 and 1519, when it was conquered by the Spanish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enchistoria_18-3"><a href="#cite_note-enchistoria-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the 15th and very early 16th century, the <a href="/wiki/Aztec" title="Aztec">Aztecs</a> came to dominate much of the state and dividing it into tributary provinces, of Tochtepec, Cuetlaxtlan, Cempoallan, Quauhtochco, Jalapa, Misantla, and Tlatlauhquitepec. The Aztecs were interested in the area's vegetation and crops such as cedars, fruit, cotton, cacao, corn, beans and vanilla. However, the Totonacs chafed under Aztec rule, with Aztec rulers from <a href="/wiki/Axayacatl" title="Axayacatl">Axayacatl</a> to <a href="/wiki/Moctezuma_II" title="Moctezuma II">Moctezuma II</a> having to send soldiers to quell rebellions. The Huastecs were subjugated more successfully by the Aztecs and relegated to the provinces of Atlan and Tochpan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schmal_15-6"><a href="#cite_note-schmal-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Colonial_period,_1519–1821"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_period.2C_1519.E2.80.931821">Colonial period, 1519–1821</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Veracruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Colonial period, 1519–1821">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Playa_Villa_Rica_desde_Quiahuiztlan01.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1932" data-file-width="2580" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Playa_Villa_Rica_desde_Quiahuiztlan01.jpeg/220px-Playa_Villa_Rica_desde_Quiahuiztlan01.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Playa_Villa_Rica_desde_Quiahuiztlan01.jpeg/330px-Playa_Villa_Rica_desde_Quiahuiztlan01.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Playa_Villa_Rica_desde_Quiahuiztlan01.jpeg/440px-Playa_Villa_Rica_desde_Quiahuiztlan01.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Playa_Villa_Rica_desde_Quiahuiztlan01.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Playa Villa Rica, where the Spanish built the first city of Veracruz</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Veracruz played an important part in the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_the_Aztec_Empire" title="Spanish conquest of the Aztec Empire">Spanish conquest of the Aztec Empire</a> by <a href="/wiki/Hern%C3%A1n_Cort%C3%A9s" title="Hernán Cortés">Hernán Cortés</a> and his expedition members. They founded Villa Rica de la Vera Cruz on May 18, 1519, as the first Spanish town in what is now Mexico. By doing so, Cortés threw off the authority of the Governor of Cuba, Diego Veláquez, and took authority from the town council (<i>cabildo</i>) of Veracruz and claim authority directly from the Spanish crown. A small contingent of the expedition remained at Veracruz, while the main body of conquerors moved inland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Totonac_people" title="Totonac people">Totonacs</a> were the first people with whom the Spanish had contact on the American mainland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schmal_15-7"><a href="#cite_note-schmal-15">[15]</a></sup> The very first contact was with Captain <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_Grijalva" title="Juan de Grijalva">Juan de Grijalva</a> on the coastline north of the present-day city of Veracruz.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enchistoria_18-4"><a href="#cite_note-enchistoria-18">[18]</a></sup> Still chafing under Aztec rule, Totonac ruler <a href="/wiki/Tlacochcalcatl" title="Tlacochcalcatl">Tlacochcalcatl</a> welcomed <a href="/wiki/Hern%C3%A1n_Cort%C3%A9s" title="Hernán Cortés">Hernán Cortés</a> and promised 50,000 warriors to help defeat <a href="/wiki/Tenochtitlan" title="Tenochtitlan">Tenochtitlan</a>. The Spanish helped the Totonacs expel Aztec tribute collectors and to seize control of some Aztec outposts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schmal_15-8"><a href="#cite_note-schmal-15">[15]</a></sup> The Spanish founded the port city of Veracruz on the coast, as the first municipality under the direct control of the king of Spain. Cortés then began his march inland to Tenochtitlan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enchistoria_18-5"><a href="#cite_note-enchistoria-18">[18]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_the_Aztec_Empire" title="Spanish conquest of the Aztec Empire">Conquest</a>, the rest of the Totonac peoples allied themselves with the Spanish, but the Huastecs, despite also being under Aztec rule, fought against them. After the fall of Tenochtitlan, Cortés sent a regiment to subdue the Huastecs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schmal_15-9"><a href="#cite_note-schmal-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the early conquest era, Cortés distributed the labor of indigenous settlements to particular conquerors in an institution known as <a href="/wiki/Encomienda" title="Encomienda">encomienda</a>. The indigenous ruler of the settlement was charged with mobilization labor and tribute that was due the holder of the encomienda. Veracruz had a number of encomiendas that changed hands a number of times, but early on came under the direct control of the Spanish crown rather than individual <i>encomenderos</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the colonial era, Veracruz was the main port of entry for immigrants from Spain, <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">African slaves</a>, and all types of luxury goods for import and export. The first group of Franciscans arrived in Veracruz in 1524, walking barefoot to the capital of the Spanish colony of <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">New Spain</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> The route between Veracruz and the Spanish capital of Mexico City, built on the site of the Aztec capital <a href="/wiki/Tenochtitlan" title="Tenochtitlan">Tenochtitlan</a>, was the key trade route during the colonial era. Much of the history of the state is involved with the port city that Cortés founded in 1519. Veracruz became the principal and often only port to export and import goods between the colony of <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">New Spain</a> and Spain itself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schmal_15-10"><a href="#cite_note-schmal-15">[15]</a></sup> To ensure the port’s monopoly, it came to have control over almost all of New Spain's Gulf coastline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enchistoria_18-6"><a href="#cite_note-enchistoria-18">[18]</a></sup> New Spain's silver and <a href="/wiki/Cochineal" title="Cochineal">cochineal</a> red dye, were the two most important exports from the port, along with chocolate, vanilla, chili peppers, and much more were exported. Imported were livestock (sheep, cows, goats, horses), wheat and other cultivars. From the Caribbean, slaves, pineapple, and sugar cane were introduced. This made the port a highly prized target for pirates during the colonial period, with attacks and sackings frequent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-khursh_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-khursh-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schmal_15-11"><a href="#cite_note-schmal-15">[15]</a></sup> This led to the building of the fort of <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_de_Ul%C3%BAa" title="San Juan de Ulúa">San Juan de Ulúa</a> and the fortification of the city overall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enchistoria_18-7"><a href="#cite_note-enchistoria-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>Much of Totonac and Huastec culture have survived the colonial period into the present day. Much of the reason for this is that the north of Veracruz is rugged with thick vegetation and relatively little of the resources the Spanish were looking for.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schmal_15-12"><a href="#cite_note-schmal-15">[15]</a></sup> Veracruz is considered to be where the "<a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">mestizo</a>" or mixed European/indigenous race began, which is a large part of Mexican cultural identity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enchistoria_18-8"><a href="#cite_note-enchistoria-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EstatuaYanga.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1394" data-file-width="929" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/EstatuaYanga.jpg/220px-EstatuaYanga.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/EstatuaYanga.jpg/330px-EstatuaYanga.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/EstatuaYanga.jpg/440px-EstatuaYanga.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EstatuaYanga.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Statue of rebel leader Yanga</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Though the Spaniards had halted the Azrtec wars and human sacrifices an unexpected problem arose. <a href="/wiki/Influenza" title="Influenza">European diseases</a> decimated the native population of the province, prompting the importation of African slaves during the colonial period, starting in the 16th century. The Spanish imported between 500,000–1,000,000 West African slaves into Mexico between 1535 and 1767 (<a href="/wiki/Miscegenation" title="Miscegenation">miscegenation</a> between indigenous and African population began almost immediately). New Spain did not have any laws prohibiting interracial marriage, hence the correct term is Afro-Mestizo, which includes all 3 races: Indigenous, African, and Spanish.</p>
<p>Runaway slaves (<i>cimarrones</i>) became problematic to public order since they frequently formed robber bands that attacked travelers on highways. Crown efforts against these groups began in earnest in the late sixteenth century, but a major rebellion broke out in 1606 in the areas of Villa Rica, Nueva Veracruz, Antón Lizardo, and the Rio Blanco area. However, the gravest of these occurred in the Orizaba area, where there were about 500 fugitive slaves. In 1609, a leader named <a href="/wiki/Gaspar_Yanga" title="Gaspar Yanga">Gaspar Yanga</a> led an insurrection against the Spanish but was defeated in battle. Unrest continued, eventually forcing the government to sign an amnesty pact and giving the Africans the right to form their own community, exacting as a condition that bandits be suppressed. This was called San Lorenzo de Zerral but today it is known as the <a href="/wiki/Yanga,_Veracruz" title="Yanga, Veracruz">municipality of Yanga</a>. This was the first time slavery was abolished in the Americas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enchistoria_18-9"><a href="#cite_note-enchistoria-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the first half of the seventeenth century, cities such as <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba,_Veracruz" title="Córdoba, Veracruz">Córdoba</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orizaba,_Veracruz" title="Orizaba, Veracruz">Orizaba</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Xalapa" title="Xalapa">Xalapa</a> were formed or expanded to protect the trade route between Mexico City and the port of Veracruz. During this time, the Spanish and mixed-race population increased as the purely indigenous population continued to fall to a fraction of pre-Conquest levels (due now to mixing, rather than disease). Almost all trade in and out of New Spain had to be with Spain except for some limited trade authorized with England and other Spanish colonies. This would stay in place until 1778, when <i>the Decreto de Libre Comercio</i>, allowing a limited free trade within Spanish-held realms, lifted many of these restrictions on trade with Europe. This would make the port more important than it had been, and led to increased prosperity for the inhabitants.</p>
<p>Outside of the port, in other areas of the province, the economy was based on agriculture, livestock, and commerce. In 1720, Xalapa organized the first trade fair, making it the center for trade between inland Mexican goods and those from abroad. This would lead to its eventual status as capital of the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enchistoria_18-10"><a href="#cite_note-enchistoria-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1746, the state was divided into the civil jurisdictions of Pánuco, Tampico, Huayacocotla, Huauchinango, Papantla, Misantla, Xalapa, Jalacingo, Veracruz, Córdoba, Orizaba, Cosamaloapan, Tuxtla, and Cotaxtla.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enchistoria_18-11"><a href="#cite_note-enchistoria-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>The port city of Veracruz, and the fort of San Juan de Ulúa, where Cortés landed three hundred years earlier, was where the loyalist soldiers of the Spanish Crown made their last stand against the independence movement in 1824.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schmal_15-13"><a href="#cite_note-schmal-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence">Independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Veracruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Veracruz.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="405" data-file-width="640" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Battle_of_Veracruz.jpg/220px-Battle_of_Veracruz.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Battle_of_Veracruz.jpg/330px-Battle_of_Veracruz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Battle_of_Veracruz.jpg/440px-Battle_of_Veracruz.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Veracruz.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Depiction of the Battle of Veracruz during the Mexican–American War</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_War_of_Independence" title="Mexican War of Independence">Mexican War of Independence</a>, there was support for the insurgents in many parts of the state, with skirmishes erupting in various parts as early as 1811. A major conspiracy against the colonial government was discovered in the port in 1812, with rebels taking <a href="/wiki/Ayahualulco" title="Ayahualulco">Ayahualulco</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ixhuac%C3%A1n,_Veracruz" title="Ixhuacán, Veracruz">Ixhuacán</a> during the same year. This forced royalist troops to withdraw to Xalapa. Eventually, this city along with the port were cut off from Mexico City. Most of the state remained in rebel hands during the rest of the war although the commercial class of the port did not support the effort. In 1821, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Juan_de_O%27Donoj%C3%BA" title="Juan de O'Donojú">Juan de O'Donojú</a>, the last <a href="/wiki/Viceroy" title="Viceroy">viceroy</a> of New Spain, came to the port to leave for Spain. However, until 1823, Spanish troops continued to occupy San Juan de Ulúa Fort. In 1826, the city would receive the first of its four titles of "heroic city" for confronting these remaining Spanish troops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enchistoria_18-12"><a href="#cite_note-enchistoria-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>While the last of the Spanish held on in San Juan de Ulúa, <a href="/wiki/Agust%C3%ADn_de_Iturbide" title="Agustín de Iturbide">Agustín de Iturbide</a> had been declared the emperor of Mexico in 1822. However, his reign quickly encountered resistance from those favoring a republican form of government, including from <a href="/wiki/Antonio_L%C3%B3pez_de_Santa_Anna" title="Antonio López de Santa Anna">Antonio López de Santa Anna</a> from his stronghold in Veracruz state. Months later, Iturbide would go into exile and Santa Anna would eventually hold nine terms as president.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schmal_15-14"><a href="#cite_note-schmal-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enchistoria_18-13"><a href="#cite_note-enchistoria-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>The French intervened in Mexico through Veracruz for the first time in the 1838, in what became the <a href="/wiki/Pastry_War" title="Pastry War">Pastry War</a>. The port was blockaded. Efforts to defend the country were coordinated from Xalapa. The port was bombarded, but eventually a settlement was reached.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enchistoria_18-14"><a href="#cite_note-enchistoria-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War" title="Mexican–American War">Mexican–American War</a>, the port was blockaded again, this time by the Americans. Initial American attempts in 1847 to land in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alvarado_(Veracruz)" title="Alvarado (Veracruz)">Alvarado</a> were checked, but the Americans then made a plan to land a few miles south of Veracruz, which surrendered after <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Veracruz" title="Siege of Veracruz">a 20-day siege</a>, defeated General <a href="/wiki/Antonio_L%C3%B3pez_de_Santa_Anna" title="Antonio López de Santa Anna">Santa Anna</a>'s forces at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cerro_Gordo" title="Battle of Cerro Gordo">Battle of Cerro Gordo</a>, and marched inland through <a href="/wiki/Xalapa" title="Xalapa">Xalapa</a> towards Mexico City, led by General <a href="/wiki/Winfield_Scott" title="Winfield Scott">Winfield Scott</a> .<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schmal_15-15"><a href="#cite_note-schmal-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enchistoria_18-15"><a href="#cite_note-enchistoria-18">[18]</a></sup> Mexico surrendered shortly after.</p>
<p>The municipalities of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tuxpan,_Veracruz" title="Tuxpan, Veracruz">Tuxpan</a> and <a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chicontepec_de_Tejada" title="es:Chicontepec de Tejada">Chicontepec</a> belonged to Puebla until 1853, when they were annexed to Veracruz to give the state its final form. In 1855, the State Government Palace was constructed. During the <a href="/wiki/Reform_War" title="Reform War">Reform War</a>, the major player was Ignacio de la Llave whose name is part of the state's official designation. In 1858, the port became the site for the liberal government under <a href="/wiki/Benito_Ju%C3%A1rez" title="Benito Juárez">Benito Juárez</a> after he was forced out of Mexico City during the Reform War. Their control of this port and its customs duties allowed liberal forces to gather resources. Conservative forces attacked the state but were repelled from both the port and Xalapa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enchistoria_18-16"><a href="#cite_note-enchistoria-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Reform War wrecked Mexico's economy and it found itself unable to pay debts it owed to Europe. As a result, Juárez cancelled Mexico's foreign debt. Spain, Britain and France, all outraged by this action, decided in October 1861 to force repayment of their loans by the occupation of the Mexican Gulf Coast. Normally, this move would have been blocked by the United States under the <a href="/wiki/Monroe_Doctrine" title="Monroe Doctrine">Monroe Doctrine</a>, however, that nation was occupied with a Civil War at the time, and the European powers believed that the Americans could not act. In December, Spanish troops commanded by general Manuel Gasset occupied the port of Veracruz, without any local resistance,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> followed a month later by French and British forces. The Spanish and the British withdrew after making deals with Juárez, but <a href="/wiki/French_intervention_in_Mexico" title="French intervention in Mexico">the French pushed on</a> to establish the reign of <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_I_of_Mexico" title="Maximilian I of Mexico">Maximilian I of Mexico</a>. However, this was short-lived and the French were expelled through Veracruz in 1866/67.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schmal_15-16"><a href="#cite_note-schmal-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1863, the state was officially named Veracruz-Llave. After the French were expelled, the state government was in the port of Veracruz. In 1878, the capital was transferred to Orizaba. It was later moved to Xalapa in 1885.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enchistoria_18-17"><a href="#cite_note-enchistoria-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>By the end of the century, many infrastructure improvements, such as roads and railways (especially the <a href="/wiki/Interoceanic_Railway_of_Mexico" title="Interoceanic Railway of Mexico">Ferrocarril Interoceánico</a>) had been completed with the major cities being Veracruz, Orizaba, Xalapa, Córdoba, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jalacingo,_Veracruz" title="Jalacingo, Veracruz">Jalacingo</a>, Chicontepec and <a href="/wiki/Tantoyuca" title="Tantoyuca">Tantoyuca</a>. The discovery of oil in the north of the state attracted foreign firms, which brought machinery needed for its extraction. These companies included Huasteca Company Petroleum and El Aguila along with American and English firms. During the same time period, uprisings against the government under <a href="/wiki/Porfirio_D%C3%ADaz" title="Porfirio Díaz">Porfirio Díaz</a> in the agricultural south of the state were brutally repressed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enchistoria_18-18"><a href="#cite_note-enchistoria-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century_to_the_present">20th century to the present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Veracruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 20th century to the present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Unrest against the Díaz regime continued until the outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Revolution" title="Mexican Revolution">Mexican Revolution</a> ousted him from power. The major event leading up to this war in Veracruz was the cigar-makers strike of 1905, when more than 5,000 workers of the "El Valle Nacional" company walked off the job. The governor, Teodora A. Dehesa, unsuccessfully tried to negotiate a settlement. The strike went on for months until the strikers won. This victory encouraged more actions, until strikes at the factories in Rio Blanco, Nogales, Santa Rosa and Contón de Orizaba resulted in <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Blanco_strike" title="Río Blanco strike">dramatic violence in January 1907</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enchistoria_18-19"><a href="#cite_note-enchistoria-18">[18]</a></sup> No major battles of the Mexican Revolution were fought in the state, though there were skirmishes and attacks on the port. By 1914 rebel Cándido Agular occupied a number of municipalities in the state and in 1917, <a href="/wiki/Venustiano_Carranza" title="Venustiano Carranza">Venustiano Carranza</a> transferred the federal government here temporarily.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enchistoria_18-20"><a href="#cite_note-enchistoria-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>On April 21, 1914 an <a href="/wiki/Tampico_Affair" title="Tampico Affair">incident involving U.S. sailors in Tampico</a> led President <a href="/wiki/Woodrow_Wilson" title="Woodrow Wilson">Woodrow Wilson</a> to land American troops in Veracruz, where they remained for six months. Mexico later responded by severing diplomatic relations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schmal_15-17"><a href="#cite_note-schmal-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the Revolution, agrarian reform, including the redistribution of land and the creation of ejidos took place here. The oil companies in the north of the state were nationalized and consolidated into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PEMEX" title="PEMEX">PEMEX</a> in the 1930s by <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A1zaro_C%C3%A1rdenas" title="Lázaro Cárdenas">Lázaro Cárdenas</a>. In the 1950s, more road construction, such as the Mexico City- Poza Rica, Veracruz-Alvarado- Coatzacoalco and Tinajas-Ciudad Aleman-Tlacoatalpan highways were constructed. The <a href="/wiki/Universidad_Veracruzana" title="Universidad Veracruzana">Universidad Veracruzana</a> was expanded as well. In 1960, the <a href="/wiki/Museo_de_Antropolog%C3%ADa_de_Xalapa" title="Museo de Antropología de Xalapa">Museum of Anthropology in Xalapa</a> was inaugurated as well as the Coatzacoalco-<a href="/wiki/Salina_Cruz" title="Salina Cruz">Salina Cruz</a> highway. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_Heriberto_Jara_International_Airport" title="General Heriberto Jara International Airport">Veracruz city international airport</a> was opened in the 1970s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enchistoria_18-21"><a href="#cite_note-enchistoria-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Veracruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Veracruz has one of Mexico’s leading economies, based on agriculture and petroleum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brittanica_14-3"><a href="#cite_note-brittanica-14">[14]</a></sup> Using relatively recent night light data and electricity consumption in comparison with Gross County Product, the informal sector of the local economy in Veracruz state is shown to have grown during the period of the Fox Administration though the regional government remained PRI. The assumption that the informal economy of Mexico is a constant 30% of total economic activity is not supported at the local level. The small amount of local spatial autocorrelation that was found suggests a few clusters of high and low literacy rates amongst municipios in Veracruz but not enough to warrant including an I-statistic as a regressor. Global spatial autocorrelation is found especially literacy at the macro-regional level which is an area for further research beyond this study. Improved literacy bolsters both the informal and formal economies in Veracruz indicating policies designed to further literacy are vital for growing the regional economy. While indigenous people are relatively poor, little evidence was found that the informal economy is a higher percentage of total economic activity in a municipio with a high share of indigenous people. While the formal economy might have been expanding relative to the informal economy in 2000, by 2006 this process had been reversed with growing informality. While rural municipios have smaller economies, they are not different than urban municipios in the share of the economy that is informal. Programs in the past that might move economic activity from the informal to the formal sector have not succeeded suggesting public finance issues such as tax evasion will continue to plague the state with low government revenues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Veracruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vanilla_beans.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1536" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Vanilla_beans.jpg/220px-Vanilla_beans.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Vanilla_beans.jpg/330px-Vanilla_beans.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Vanilla_beans.jpg/440px-Vanilla_beans.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vanilla_beans.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Vanilla beans</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The primary sector of the economy (agriculture, forestry and fishing) has been important since pre-Hispanic times and continues to be important both as a source of income as well as culturally. The state has abundant rainfall and extremely fertile soils, as well as a long coastline and forest containing a wide variety of trees and other plants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schmal_15-18"><a href="#cite_note-schmal-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moritzky_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-moritzky-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>There is about 1 million hectares of cultivable land, half of which is in private hands and 43% is <a href="/wiki/Ejido" title="Ejido">ejido</a> or communal land. The rest is occupied by human settlements. There are 3,620 ejidos parceled out to 270,000 ejido members. 52.5% of agricultural land is used for the growing of crops or used as pasture and 43.1% is forest or rainforest. Chief agricultural products include coffee, vanilla, sugarcane, tobacco, bananas, coconuts, and vegetables, but local farmers depend mainly on corn and beans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brittanica_14-4"><a href="#cite_note-brittanica-14">[14]</a></sup> Two corn crops per year are generally produced, planted on 644,936 hectares with a production of 1,114,325 tons. The state is the leading national producer of coffee, sugarcane, corn, and rice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schmal_15-19"><a href="#cite_note-schmal-15">[15]</a></sup> Coffee is grown on 152,993 hectares producing 400,575 tons. Export earnings from this crop are about 232 million USD annually. Most coffee is grown in the mountain areas of Córdoba-Huatusco, Coatepec-Teocelo-Cosautlán and Misantla-Tlapacoyan-Atzalan. Sugarcane is cultivated on 254,000 hectares, producing 16,867,958 tons annually. Veracruz is the largest producer of rice with 24,000 hectares producing 120,000 tons. Much is this crop is protected by import bans from Asia.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The state grows half of the country’s citrus fruit and grows the most kinds. This occupies 180,577 hectares and produces 2,575,140 tons annually. Varieties include oranges, <a href="/wiki/Tangerine" title="Tangerine">tangerines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_orange" title="Mandarin orange">mandarins</a>, limes and grapefruit. Most citrus is grown in the north of the state, and much of the lime crop is exported, supporting a packing and shipping industry. Veracruz is the largest <a href="/wiki/Mango" title="Mango">mango</a> producer in the country, grown on 31,640 hectares producing 287,000 tons. Most of this is the manila variety, which is preferred in Mexico. 95% of this crop is consumed fresh within Mexico although exports to Canada have begun.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Vanilla beans are native to the state, which is the primary producer for Mexico. Most of this crop is grown in an area known as Totonacapan in and around Papantla.</p>
<p>Livestock raising is an important activity. There are over 300,000 units of production most of which raise cattle, with Veracruz being the main beef producer for the country at 14% of the total. In addition to beef cattle, dairy cattle, pigs, sheep, goats, horses, domestic fowl, and bees are raised.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brittanica_14-5"><a href="#cite_note-brittanica-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>From the tropical forests of the inland regions come <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dyewood" title="Dyewood">dyewoods</a>, hardwoods, and rubber.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schmal_15-20"><a href="#cite_note-schmal-15">[15]</a></sup> About 20% of the state’s territory is forested, with 220,000 of temperate forest and 1,200,000 hectares of tropical forests. Logging in the state produces 128,254 m3 of wood products per year. The most exploited species include pine, oyamel, cypress and oak. Some tropical hardwoods are harvested as well.</p>
<p>Veracruz’s long coastline supports a large fishing industry, producing one-fifth of Mexico’s catch. Most of the country’s <a href="/wiki/Mojarra" title="Mojarra">mojarra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oyster" title="Oyster">oysters</a> and shrimp come from here. Other major fish catches include crab, <a href="/wiki/White_seabass" title="White seabass">sea bass</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_red_snapper" title="Northern red snapper">red snapper</a>.</p>
<p>Agroindustry focuses on the processing of coffee and sugar products, with citrus packers holding an important position as well.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_resources">Natural resources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Veracruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Natural resources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Torre_Petrolera_Poza_Rica.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1023" data-file-width="767" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Torre_Petrolera_Poza_Rica.jpg/100px-Torre_Petrolera_Poza_Rica.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Torre_Petrolera_Poza_Rica.jpg/150px-Torre_Petrolera_Poza_Rica.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Torre_Petrolera_Poza_Rica.jpg/200px-Torre_Petrolera_Poza_Rica.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Torre_Petrolera_Poza_Rica.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Petroleum tower in Poza Rica</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Today, the state of Veracruz, rich in natural resources, is an important component of Mexico's economy. Approximately 35% of Mexico's water supply is found in Veracruz. There are a number of metallic and non-metallic mineral mining but the most important resource is oil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schmal_15-21"><a href="#cite_note-schmal-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>The mountains contain relatively unexploited deposits of gold, silver, iron, and coal. Although Veracruz is an important source of metals such as iron and copper, a great deal of its mining involves non-metallic minerals as sulfur, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Silica" title="Silica">silica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Feldspar" title="Feldspar">feldspar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Calcium" title="Calcium">calcium</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kaolin" title="Kaolin">kaolin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marble" title="Marble">marble</a>. The state is ranked fourth in the nation for this kind of mining production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediofisico_13-11"><a href="#cite_note-mediofisico-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schmal_15-22"><a href="#cite_note-schmal-15">[15]</a></sup> However, mining only accounts for 1.5% of economic activity for the entire state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schmal_15-23"><a href="#cite_note-schmal-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Veracruz was a pioneer in both the extraction and refining of petroleum products.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediofisico_13-12"><a href="#cite_note-mediofisico-13">[13]</a></sup> The state has about one-fourth of Mexico’s petroleum reserves and ranks third in petroleum production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediofisico_13-13"><a href="#cite_note-mediofisico-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brittanica_14-6"><a href="#cite_note-brittanica-14">[14]</a></sup> Most of this production is concentrated in the northern part of the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schmal_15-24"><a href="#cite_note-schmal-15">[15]</a></sup> Approximately 40,000,000 barrels (6,400,000 m<sup>3</sup>) of oil are produced each year and 109,870,000,000 cubic feet (3.111<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">×</span>10<sup>9</sup> m<sup>3</sup>) of natural gas. Petrochemicals represent 28.1% of the state’s manufacturing and ranks first nationally. There are 22 petrochemical plants, with the most important being <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=La_Cangrejera&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="La Cangrejera (page does not exist)">La Cangrejera</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/J%C3%A1ltipan_de_Morelos" title="Jáltipan de Morelos">Jáltipan de Morelos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poza_Rica" title="Poza Rica">Poza Rica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cosoleacaque" title="Cosoleacaque">Cosoleacaque</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pajaritos,_Veracruz&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Pajaritos, Veracruz (page does not exist)">Pajaritos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Minatitl%C3%A1n,_Veracruz" title="Minatitlán, Veracruz">Minatitlán</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Golden_Lane_Oil_Fields">Golden Lane Oil Fields</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Veracruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Golden Lane Oil Fields">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Golden_Lane_Map.pdf"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1247" data-file-width="961" height="389" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Golden_Lane_Map.pdf/page1-300px-Golden_Lane_Map.pdf.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Golden_Lane_Map.pdf/page1-450px-Golden_Lane_Map.pdf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Golden_Lane_Map.pdf/page1-600px-Golden_Lane_Map.pdf.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Golden_Lane_Map.pdf" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of the Golden Lane<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The "Golden Lane" ("Dos Bocas-Alamo structure" or The Ridge") refers to a series of oil fields aligned in an arc onshore and a symmetrical alignment offshore, forming two sides of a <a href="/wiki/Cretaceous" title="Cretaceous">Cretaceous</a> <a href="/wiki/Atoll" title="Atoll">atoll</a> 180 km long.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Viniegra_O._p._309_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Viniegra_O._p._309-26">[26]</a></sup> The structure was discovered in 1908 by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weetman_Pearson" title="Weetman Pearson">Weetman Pearson</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Eagle_Petroleum_Company" title="Mexican Eagle Petroleum Company">Mexican Eagle Petroleum Company</a> San diego de la Mar No. 1 well, which flowed 2,500 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bbl" title="Bbl">bbl</a>/day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Viniegra_O._p._309_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-Viniegra_O._p._309-26">[26]</a></sup> The Golden Lane oil fields penetrate a massive elliptical <a href="/wiki/Reef" title="Reef">reef</a> platform, identified as the Sierra del Abra limestone (consisting of reef, backreef and <a href="/wiki/Lagoon" title="Lagoon">lagoonal</a> <a href="/wiki/Facies" title="Facies">facies</a>), which dips southeast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> The site for the discovery well was selected due to the presence of <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_seep" title="Petroleum seep">petroleum seeps</a>, just as was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Edward_Laurence_Doheny" title="Edward Laurence Doheny">Edward Laurence Doheny</a>'s La Paz No. well in the Ebano-Panuco petroleum district west of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tampico,_Tamaulipas" title="Tampico, Tamaulipas">Tampico, Tamaulipas</a>, the first Mexican discovery well in 1904.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> In 1908, the infamous <a href="/wiki/Dos_Bocas_oil_fire" title="Dos Bocas oil fire">Dos Bocas oil fire</a> occurred after the San Diego de la Mar No. 3 <a href="/wiki/Blowout_(well_drilling)" title="Blowout (well drilling)">blowout</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Viniegra_O._p._311_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Viniegra_O._p._311-29">[29]</a></sup> This was followed by the Potrero del Llano No. 4 well, flowing 100,000 bbl per day during the three months it was out of control.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Viniegra_O._p._311_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-Viniegra_O._p._311-29">[29]</a></sup> Doheny's Cerro Azul No. 4 well, located by Ezequiel Ordonez, became the largest daily production record holder in 1916 at 260,000 bbl.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Viniegra_O._p._311_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-Viniegra_O._p._311-29">[29]</a></sup> Geophysical studies, in particular <a href="/wiki/Gravimetry" title="Gravimetry">gravimetry</a>, starting in 1920 led to the discovery of the Poza Rica Field in 1932 and Moralillo Field in 1948, on the west flank of the Golden Lane in the Tamabra forereef facies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Refraction <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seismography" title="Seismography">seismography</a> surveys started in 1930, augemented in 1948 with reflection seismography, which led to the discovery of the southern extent of the atoll with the Ezequiel Ordonez No. 1 well in 1952 and additional discoveries through 1968.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Viniegra_O._p._312_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Viniegra_O._p._312-31">[31]</a></sup> Marine seismic and <a href="/wiki/Magnetometer" title="Magnetometer">magnetometer</a> surveys starting in 1957 showed the extent of the atoll offshore and led to the first offshore well, Isla de Lobos No. 1-B, in 1963.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Viniegra_O._p._312_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-Viniegra_O._p._312-31">[31]</a></sup> The depths of wells are on the order of 500 m onshore and 2000 m offshore.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Industry,_transportation_and_commerce"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry.2C_transportation_and_commerce">Industry, transportation and commerce</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Veracruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Industry, transportation and commerce">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Laguna_Verde_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Laguna Verde Nuclear Power Plant">Laguna Verde Nuclear Power Plant</a> (LVNPP) in Alto Lucero, Veracruz, produces about 4.5% of Mexico's electrical energy.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PortVeracruz55.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/PortVeracruz55.JPG/220px-PortVeracruz55.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/PortVeracruz55.JPG/330px-PortVeracruz55.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/PortVeracruz55.JPG/440px-PortVeracruz55.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PortVeracruz55.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A portion of the port of Veracruz</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The manufacturing industry in Veracruz accounts for between 21% and one-third of the state's gross domestic product, and approximately 64% of the manufacturing industry GDP is generated by the chemical and petrochemical sectors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schmal_15-25"><a href="#cite_note-schmal-15">[15]</a></sup> Other products produced include metals, processed foods, beverages, printing and publishing, textiles and machinery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schmal_15-26"><a href="#cite_note-schmal-15">[15]</a></sup> Most of the state's industry takes place in the municipalities of <a href="/wiki/Coatzacoalcos" title="Coatzacoalcos">Coatzacoalcos</a>, Minatitlán, Cosoleacaque, Poza Rica, Córdoba, Orizaba, Tuxpan and Veracruz, with over 5,000 establishments. The rest is divided among nearly 11,000 smaller establishments. There are five major industrial parks: Bruno Pagliai, Ixtac, Petroquimico Morelos, Córdoba-Amatlán and Parque 2000. The largest of these is Bruno Pagliai, which covers 300.8 hectares.</p>
